  * *using software such as graphic organisers to determine a fundamental cause of a problem or to represent related elements of a problem that need to be jointly addressed in the <strong>digital solution</strong>*
  * *testing a range of text and graphical user interface designs with clients who have different needs on the basis of time taken to complete the task and the number of errors made*
* <span class="light">**DT 9-10**: Evaluate critically how student solutions and existing <strong>information</strong> systems and policies, take account of future risks and sustainability and provide opportunities for innovation and enterprise
 (ACTDIP042)</span>
  * *investigating actions, devices and events that are potential risks to <strong>information</strong> systems, for example losing portable storage devices containing important files, deliberately infecting systems through malware, and power surges*
* <span class="light">**DT 9-10**: Create interactive solutions for sharing ideas and <strong>information</strong> online, taking into account safety, social contexts and legal responsibilities (ACTDIP043)</span>
  * *creating online interactive solutions for working with others by combining or modifying online software tools to support project work*
* <span class="light">**HPE 9-10**: Provide and apply feedback to develop and refine specialised movement skills in a range of challenging movement situations (ACPMP099)</span>
  * *providing constructive feedback on their own and others' performance by using movement-analysis software to break down a skill or sequence*
* <span class="light">**Hist 9**: Select and use a range of communication forms (oral, graphic, written) and <strong>digital technologies</strong> (ACHHS175)</span>
  * *using online conferencing and other forms of <strong>ICT</strong> to discuss historical questions and issues*
* <span class="light">**Geo 10**: Evaluate sources for their reliability, bias and usefulness and select, collect, record and organise relevant geographical <strong>data</strong> and <strong>information</strong>, using ethical protocols, from a range of appropriate primary and secondary sources
 (ACHGS073)</span>
  * *using Gapminder or United Nations statistics to collect <strong>data</strong> on countries to answer an inquiry question*

### Understand ICT systems

#### **Level 2**: identify the main components of common consumer ICT systems, their fundamental functions, and describe them using basic ICT terminology

##### Content descriptions

* **DT F-2**: Recognise and explore <strong>digital systems</strong> (hardware and software components) for a purpose (ACTDIK001)
  * *playing with and using different <strong>digital systems</strong> for transferring and capturing <strong>data</strong>, for example using a tablet to take a photograph of a grandparent and recording an interview with them about life in the past*
  * *exploring and using <strong>digital systems</strong> for downloading and storing <strong>information</strong>, for example knowing how to download images from a <strong>website</strong> and inserting them into a document; saving and retrieving <strong>data</strong>*
  * *exploring and identifying hardware and software components of <strong>digital systems</strong> when creating ideas and <strong>information</strong>, for example experimenting with different ways of providing instructions to games software using a mouse, touch pad, touch screen, keyboard, stylus, or switch scanning device, and using different software to manipulate text, numbers, sound and images*
  * *recognising and using hardware and software components of <strong>digital systems</strong> and experimenting with their functions, for example playing with interactive toys and robotic devices to determine which ones can work with other devices*
  * *recognising that a <strong>digital system</strong> follows instructions or commands, for example instructing robotic toys to perform a function such as a dance movement*
* **DT F-2**: Explore how people safely use common <strong>information</strong> systems to meet <strong>information</strong>, communication and recreation needs (ACTDIP005)
  * *sharing and describing ways that common <strong>information</strong> systems can be used to meet communication needs, for example computers can be used as phones and social networking tools allowing communication between families living in different regions*
  * *recognising safe ergonomic practices when children are playing with <strong>information</strong> systems, for example recognising the need to take regular breaks to avoid eye strain and repetitive strain injuries*
  * *discussing how a range of <strong>information</strong> systems support personal needs and impact on others, for example text to speech software for people with vision loss*
  * *sharing ideas about the ways <strong>information</strong> systems are being used by families and friends in everyday life, for example comparing current <strong>digital play</strong> equipment with play equipment of 20 years ago*
* **DT F-2**: Create and organise ideas and <strong>information</strong> using <strong>information</strong> systems independently and with others, and share these with known people in safe online environments (ACTDIP006)

##### Elaborations only

* <span class="light">**Media F-2**: Use media technologies to capture and edit images, sounds and text for a purpose (ACAMAM055)</span>
  * *practising using computer software to add captions to images to enhance meaning in a photo story*

#### **Level 3**: identify and compare the use of the main components of different ICT systems

##### Content descriptions

* **DT 3-4**: Identify and explore a range of <strong>digital systems</strong> with peripheral devices for different purposes, and transmit different types of <strong>data</strong>
 (ACTDIK007)
  * *experimenting with different types of <strong>digital system</strong> components and peripheral devices to perform input, output and storage functions, for example a keyboard, stylus, touch screen, switch scan device or joystick to input instructions; a monitor, printer or tablet to display <strong>information</strong>; a USB flash drive and external hard drive as storage peripheral devices*
  * *recognising that images and music can be transferred from a mobile device to a computer, for example using a cable to connect a camera and computer to upload images for a photo story*
* **DT 3-4**: Recognise different types of <strong>data</strong> and explore how the same <strong>data</strong> can be represented in different ways (ACTDIK008)
  * *recognising that numbers, text, images, sounds, animations and videos are all forms of <strong>data</strong> when stored or viewed using a <strong>digital system</strong>*

##### Elaborations only

* <span class="light">**DT 3-4**: Implement simple <strong>digital solutions</strong> as visual programs with algorithms involving branching (decisions) and user input
 (ACTDIP011)</span>
  * *exploring common elements of standard user interfaces that are familiar and appeal to users, for example navigation links on the left and top of <strong>web pages</strong> to help users interact with the site*
* <span class="light">**DT 3-4**: Explain how student solutions and existing <strong>information</strong> systems meet common personal, school or community needs (ACTDIP012)</span>
  * *investigating how <strong>information</strong> systems are used in communities and explaining what needs are being met, for example students jointly creating a short survey and collecting <strong>data</strong> about how many community residents use the online library borrowing system to download e-books and why they do or do not*
  * *exploring <strong>information</strong> systems that suit particular home or personal needs, for example  using speech recognition software that can help speakers whose language background is not English, or a system to monitor energy or water consumption in the home*
  * *testing the adequacy of student solutions, for example asking a classmate to review a <strong>digital solution</strong> and provide feedback*
* <span class="light">**DT 3-4**: Plan, create and communicate ideas and <strong>information</strong> independently and with others, applying agreed ethical and social protocols
 (ACTDIP013)</span>
  * *considering ways of managing the use of social media to maintain privacy needs, for example activating privacy settings to avoid divulging personal <strong>data</strong> such as photographs, addresses, and names and recognising that all <strong>digital interactions</strong> are difficult to erase (<strong>digital footprints</strong>)*
  * *using a range of online tools to share <strong>information</strong> and being aware that <strong>information</strong> may be received at different times, for example adding entries to a class blog, participating in a web conference or online chat with an author, or participating in a forum on a specific topic*
  * *organising and creating different types of <strong>information</strong> for sharing and collaborating online, for example planning the sequence and appearance of an animation, and sharing it online with students from another school*
  * *managing a project that involves students working together to publish online, for example identifying how group members can help each other to avoid delays in finishing the project*

#### **Level 4**: identify, compare and classify basic ICT system components

##### Content descriptions

* **DT 5-6**: Examine the main components of common <strong>digital systems</strong> and how they may connect together to form networks to transmit <strong>data</strong>
 (ACTDIK014)
  * *describing <strong>digital systems</strong> as having internal and external components that perform different functions, for example external components for inputting <strong>data</strong> including keyboard, microphone, stylus; internal processing components including the central processing unit; external output components including speakers, projector, screen; and <strong>data</strong> and <strong>information</strong> storage components including cloud and external devices*
  * *explaining how <strong>data</strong> may be transmitted between two <strong>digital systems</strong> in different ways, for example that wires or cables are used in wired networks to transfer <strong>data</strong> from one <strong>digital system</strong> to another, and radio waves are used to transmit <strong>data</strong> in wireless or mobile networks*
  * *investigating how the internal and external components of <strong>digital systems</strong> are coordinated to handle <strong>data</strong>, for example how a keyboard, central processing unit and screen work together to accept, manipulate and present <strong>data</strong> and <strong>information</strong>*
  * *investigating how emerging <strong>digital systems</strong> work, for example using an augmented reality app (or blended reality) and considering how images of real-world objects can be blended with computer-generated <strong>information</strong> to produce a <strong>virtual reality</strong>*
* **DT 5-6**: Acquire, store and validate different types of <strong>data</strong>, and use a range of software to interpret and visualise <strong>data</strong> to create <strong>information</strong> (ACTDIP016)
  * *using <strong>digital systems</strong> to validate <strong>data</strong>, for example setting <strong>data</strong> types in a spreadsheet to make sure a date is input correctly*
  * *recognising the difference between numerical, text and date formats in spreadsheets*
  * *using software to automate calculations to help with interpreting <strong>data</strong>, for example using functions to make arithmetic calculations using multiple cells and summing cell ranges*
  * *acquiring <strong>data</strong> from online sources by narrowing the focus, for example filtering <strong>data</strong> using provided options or performing queries using advanced search functions*
  * *using <strong>data</strong> visualisation software to help in interpreting trends, for example uploading <strong>data</strong> to a web application and building a visualisation of the <strong>data</strong>set*
* **DT 5-6**: Explain how student solutions and existing <strong>information</strong> systems are sustainable and meet current and future local community needs (ACTDIP021)
  * *imagining how the functioning of one type of <strong>information</strong> system could be applied in a new way to meet a community or national need, for example considering how an electronic tracking system such as a global positioning system (GPS) could be used to find people who are lost*
  * *comparing past and present <strong>information</strong> systems in terms of economic, environmental and social sustainability, including those of Aboriginal and Torres Strait Islander Peoples*
  * *considering opportunities and consequences of decisions for future applications, for example practices to save energy and other resources when using <strong>information</strong> systems, such as switching off when not in use, ensuring electronic devices are in energy-saving mode*

##### Elaborations only

* <span class="light">**D&T 5-6**: Investigate how electrical energy can control movement, sound or light in a designed product or system
 (ACTDEK020)</span>
  * *producing models using materials, tools and equipment to show how to control movement, sound or light*
* <span class="light">**DT 5-6**: Define problems in terms of <strong>data</strong> and functional requirements drawing on previously solved problems (ACTDIP017)</span>
  * *investigating characteristics of user interfaces that are common for particular types of problems, for example, touch screens – many people respond more intuitively than when using a keyboard or stylus; and the consistent placement of symbols helps with performing actions that require speed, for example in games*
* <span class="light">**DT 5-6**: Design a user interface for a <strong>digital system</strong>
 (ACTDIP018)</span>
  * *designing the user interface of a solution using different design tools, for example using a storyboard to outline the stages of a game or a mock-up to show the placement of icons*
* <span class="light">**DT 5-6**: Plan, create and communicate ideas and <strong>information</strong>, including collaboratively online, applying agreed ethical, social and technical protocols (ACTDIP022)</span>
  * *applying safe practices while participating in online environments, for example checking the default privacy settings to ensure maximum protection of personal details, being aware of online filtering techniques and policies used at school and at home*
  * *using <strong>digital systems</strong> to create web-based <strong>information</strong> taking into consideration referencing conventions, for example creating a blog, <strong>website</strong> or online learning space for sharing ideas*

#### **Level 5**: identify and compare networked ICT system components including between hardware, software and data

##### Content descriptions

* **DT 7-8**: Investigate how <strong>data</strong> is transmitted and secured in wired, wireless and mobile networks, and how the specifications affect performance (ACTDIK023)
  * *explaining that networks have components that control the movement of <strong>data</strong>, for example routers, hubs, switches and bridges manage <strong>data</strong> traffic and that the characteristics of these components impact on the operation (speed and security) of networks*
  * *explaining how cellular radio towers (transceivers) and mobile phones work together to create mobile networks*
  * *comparing the reliability and speed of transmitting <strong>data</strong> through wireless, wired and mobile networks*
  * *recognising that there are different communications protocols for transmitting <strong>data</strong> in networks, for example hypertext transfer protocol (HTTP) is used for transferring <strong>web page</strong> files in a browser, file transfer protocol (FTP) is used for sending and receiving any files over a network and transmission control protocol/<strong>internet</strong> protocol (TCP/IP) is used for controlling file transfers over the <strong>internet</strong>*
* **DT 7-8**: Investigate how <strong>digital systems</strong> represent text, image and audio <strong>data</strong> in binary
 (ACTDIK024)
  * *explaining that characters in text correspond to numbers defined by the character set, for example ‘A’ corresponds to 65 in the ASCII and Unicode character sets*
  * *recognising that Unicode attempts to represent the written symbols of every language; and using Unicode charts to look up characters from Asian writing systems*
  * *investigating the different representation of bitmap and vector graphics and its consequences, for example pixelation in magnified bitmap and vector images*
  * *investigating how colours are represented in images and videos, for example manipulating red, green and blue (RGB) colours in an image editor*
  * *converting between decimal and 8-bit (1 byte) unsigned binary, covering whole numbers typically used for characters and RGB, for example 65 in decimal is 01000001 in 8-bit binary*
  * *explaining ways media elements are presented, for example the difference between embedded and linked media elements*
* **DT 7-8**: Analyse and visualise <strong>data</strong> using a range of software to create <strong>information</strong>, and use structured <strong>data</strong> to model objects or events (ACTDIP026)
  * *using features and functions of software to summarise <strong>data</strong> to create <strong>information</strong>, for example calculating a simple budget of income and payments and creating a summary table for analysis*
* **DT 7-8**: Design the user experience of a <strong>digital system</strong>, generating, evaluating and communicating alternative designs (ACTDIP028)
  * *designing the user interface of a solution using a range of design tools, for example using a storyboard to explain the stages of a game, and wire-frames and mock-ups to describe the appearance of a solution*
  * *identifying features that make an effective game, such as storyline, goal, reward, gameplay and environment*
  * *identifying similar <strong>digital systems</strong> and their user interfaces, assessing whether user interface elements can be re-used*
  * *presenting and comparing alternative designs to a solution for a problem, for example presenting alternative design mock-ups to the class*
  * *applying the principles and elements of design to a series of solutions to evaluate the success of each solution to hold the viewer’s attention, for example identifying which colour combinations or framing of visual elements keep different audiences engaged with on-screen activity*
* **DT 7-8**: Evaluate how student solutions and existing <strong>information</strong> systems meet needs, are innovative, and take account of future risks and sustainability (ACTDIP031)
  * *comparing student solutions with existing solutions that solve similar problems, for example identifying differences in the user interface of two adventure games and explaining how these differences affect the usability or appeal of the game*
  * *investigating what features of touch input rather than keyboard or mouse input contribute to their success in meeting a wide range of needs, for example mimicking a common movement such as expanding or contracting a hand to change the size of an object on screen, suits users with a range of dexterity*
  * *evaluating the success of <strong>information</strong> systems in meeting an economic, environmental or social objective, for example interviewing a local business owner to find out how effectively their <strong>information</strong> system supports a business objective such as increasing market share*
  * *considering the effects of e-waste on societies and environments, for example the impacts of toxic chemicals when hardware is disposed of, and the practice of dumping unwanted <strong>digital systems</strong> overseas, particularly in the Asia region*
  * *comparing cloud-based <strong>information</strong> systems to client-based <strong>information</strong> systems*

##### Elaborations only

* <span class="light">**D&T 7-8**: Analyse how motion, force and energy are used to manipulate and control electromechanical systems when designing simple, engineered solutions (ACTDEK031)</span>
  * *calculating an engineered system’s outputs, for example speed, brightness of light, volume of sound*
  * *producing prototypes and jigs to test functionality, including the use of rapid prototyping tools such as 3D printers*
  * *using code to control systems, for example code to program a microcontroller or a simple, object-based coding application to program a system such as a remote-controlled car or simple robotic arm*
  * *investigating components, tools and equipment, for example testing the durability of batteries, determining the effective range of wireless devices*
* <span class="light">**D&T 7-8**: Critique needs or opportunities for designing and investigate, analyse and select from a range of materials, components, tools, equipment and processes to develop design ideas (ACTDEP035)</span>
  * *investigating emerging technologies and their potential impact on design decisions, for example flame retardant fabrics or smart materials such as self-healing materials, <strong>digital technologies</strong> and agriculture*
* <span class="light">**D&T 7-8**: Use project management processes when working individually and collaboratively to coordinate production of designed solutions (ACTDEP039)</span>
  * *explaining and interpreting drawings, planning and production steps needed to produce products, services or environments for specific purposes*
* <span class="light">**DT 7-8**: Acquire <strong>data</strong> from a range of sources and evaluate authenticity, accuracy and timeliness (ACTDIP025)</span>
  * *designing a search engine query to find specific <strong>information</strong> on the web and checking its accuracy against <strong>information</strong> contained in other sources, for example entering instructions such as*
* <span class="light">**DT 7-8**: Define and decompose real-world problems taking into account functional requirements and economic, environmental, social, technical and usability constraints (ACTDIP027)</span>
  * *starting from a simplified system, gradually increase complexity until a model of a real-world system is developed, and record the difficulties associated with each stage of implementation*
* <span class="light">**DT 7-8**: Implement and modify programs with user interfaces involving branching, iteration and functions in a general-purpose programming language (ACTDIP030)</span>
  * *developing and modifying <strong>digital solutions</strong> by implementing instructions contained in algorithms through programs*
  * *creating <strong>digital solutions</strong> that provide user navigation and prompts with controlled repetitions, for example an <strong>information</strong> kiosk that has layers of buttons and prompts the user three times before returning to the beginning*
* <span class="light">**DT 7-8**: Plan and manage projects that create and communicate ideas and <strong>information</strong> collaboratively online, taking safety and social contexts into account (ACTDIP032)</span>
  * *creating web-based <strong>information</strong> to meet specific needs, for example modifying an existing <strong>website</strong> template or using web-authoring software including using HTML and cascading style sheets (CSS) to create a <strong>website</strong> that allows customers to interact with an enterprising solution*
* <span class="light">**Hist 7**: Use a range of communication forms (oral, graphic, written) and <strong>digital technologies</strong> (ACHHS214)</span>
  * *creating an audiovisual presentation, using <strong>ICT</strong>, to recreate and show the specific features of an ancient battle, temple, pyramid complex or burial site*
* <span class="light">**Hist 8**: Use a range of communication forms (oral, graphic, written) and <strong>digital technologies</strong> (ACHHS157)</span>
  * *creating an oral presentation, supported by audiovisual material, to recount the life of Temujin (Genghis Khan) and to explain his contribution to the Mongol world*

#### **Level 6**: apply an understanding of networked ICT system components to make changes to functions, processes, procedures and devices to fit the purpose of the solutions

##### Content descriptions

* **D&T 9-10**: Explain how products, services and environments evolve with consideration of preferred futures and the impact of emerging technologies on design decisions (ACTDEK041)
* **DT 9-10**: Investigate the role of hardware and software in managing, controlling and securing the movement of and access to <strong>data</strong> in networked <strong>digital systems</strong> (ACTDIK034)
  * *explaining how an operating system manages the relationship between hardware, applications and system software*
  * *comparing the similarities and differences of two common operating systems*
  * *identifying how changes to the configuration of an operating system change the operation of hardware and software components in a networked <strong>digital system</strong>*
  * *explaining the role of hardware and software components in allowing people to interact with <strong>digital systems</strong>, for example using a mouse or touch pad or screen, speech, accelerometer*
  * *investigating the operation and use of robotic process control systems*
  * *explaining encryption of <strong>data</strong> as a means of protecting <strong>data</strong>, for example secret keys and ‘exclusive or’ (XOR) and hashing algorithms to <strong>digitally</strong> sign <strong>data</strong>*
* **DT 9-10**: Analyse simple compression of <strong>data</strong> and how content <strong>data</strong> are separated from presentation (ACTDIK035)
  * *explaining how simple compression schemes reduce the size of repetitive <strong>data</strong>, for example how run length encoding reduces the size of images*
  * *explaining the difference between lossy and lossless compression, for example the difference between JPEG and PNG images*
  * *explaining codecs for audio-visual compression, for example common codecs for video formats*
  * *generating a layout or report in a <strong>data</strong>base or applying a style sheet to a <strong>web page</strong>*
* **DT 9-10**: Design the user experience of a <strong>digital system</strong> by evaluating alternative designs against criteria including functionality, accessibility, usability, and aesthetics
 (ACTDIP039)
  * *designing the user interface of a solution using story boards and mock-ups, for example mocking up the product design of an app for people with disability*
  * *identifying similar <strong>digital systems</strong> and existing user interfaces, assessing whether their elements can be reused*
  * *evaluating aspects of the total user experience, that is, all aspects of the system as perceived by the users, for example, a user’s initial experience of setting up and using a system, or a user’s emotional or cultural response to using a <strong>digital system</strong>*
  * *applying the principles and elements of design to a client’s requirements and evaluating the success of a solution through an iterative feedback process, for example using customer feedback to refine a user interface to more effectively provide access to important features*
* **DT 9-10**: Evaluate critically how student solutions and existing <strong>information</strong> systems and policies, take account of future risks and sustainability and provide opportunities for innovation and enterprise
 (ACTDIP042)
  * *investigating actions, devices and events that are potential risks to <strong>information</strong> systems, for example losing portable storage devices containing important files, deliberately infecting systems through malware, and power surges*
  * *investigating techniques used by people and organisations to shape how <strong>information</strong> systems are used, for example refusing to use innovations, using social media to advocate behaviours, purchasing devices, withdrawing previous processes that can now only be performed by an <strong>information</strong> system*
  * *investigating the impact and opportunities created through the practice of planned obsolescence, for example discussing the benefits and risks to users, the creators and the environment of <strong>information</strong> systems having a defined life span, taking into account costs, research and resource extraction*

##### Elaborations only

* <span class="light">**D&T 9-10**: Investigate and make judgements on how the characteristics and properties of materials, systems, components, tools and equipment can be combined to create designed solutions (ACTDEK046)</span>
  * *justifying decisions when selecting from a broad range of technologies − materials, systems, components, tools and equipment, for example selecting low-emission paints and locally sourced materials*
* <span class="light">**D&T 9-10**: Critically analyse factors, including social, ethical and sustainability considerations, that impact on designed solutions for global preferred futures and the complex design and production processes involved (ACTDEK040)</span>
  * *explaining how product life cycle thinking can influence decision-making related to design and technologies, for example rethinking products to provide for re-use, selecting a material for a product that has a lower carbon footprint*
  * *critiquing mass production systems taking into account ethics and sustainability considerations, for example the mass production of food, clothing and shoes and why manufacturers produce different versions of the same product*
* <span class="light">**D&T 9-10**: Investigate and make judgements on how the characteristics and properties of materials are combined with force, motion and energy to create engineered solutions (ACTDEK043)</span>
  * *critiquing the effectiveness of the combinations of materials, forces, energy and motion in an engineered system such as a 3D printer*
* <span class="light">**D&T 9-10**: Investigate and make judgements, within a range of technologies specialisations, on how technologies can be combined to create designed solutions (ACTDEK047)</span>
  * *critiquing product manufacturing processes in relation to society, ethics, and sustainability factors, for example a mechanised entertainment system; an interactive <strong>multimedia</strong> product to teach a concept to a student in a country in Asia*
* <span class="light">**DT 9-10**: Create interactive solutions for sharing ideas and <strong>information</strong> online, taking into account safety, social contexts and legal responsibilities (ACTDIP043)</span>
  * *investigating legal responsibilities of organisations regarding the storage, communication and disposal of personal and organisational <strong>data</strong>, for example the Australian Privacy Principles as they apply to intellectual property*
  * *applying techniques to make ethical decisions when faced with dilemmas about security and ownership of <strong>data</strong>, for example selecting an action that results in the greatest benefit for the most number of people; avoiding the use of photos of deceased persons from Aboriginal and Torres Strait Islander communities*
* <span class="light">**DT 9-10**: Plan and manage projects using an iterative and collaborative approach, identifying risks and considering safety and sustainability (ACTDIP044)</span>
  * *managing and modifying the development of a solution, for example using software to record and monitor project tasks, responsibilities and timeframes and to organise continuous opportunities to review progress with collaborative partners and to conduct regular unit testing*

### Manage digital data

#### **Level 2**: manage and maintain digital data with guidance

##### Content descriptions

* **DT F-2**: Collect, explore and sort <strong>data</strong>, and use <strong>digital systems</strong> to present the <strong>data</strong> creatively (ACTDIP003)
  * *collecting, and sorting <strong>data</strong> through play, for example collecting <strong>data</strong> about favourite toys and sorting them into categories such as toys they like or dislike*
  * *locating and purposefully using visual or text <strong>data</strong>, for example searching through a <strong>digital photo</strong> library to select an image, taking into account cultural considerations such as awareness of appropriate use of images and audio recordings of deceased persons*
  * *exploring, imagining and comparing the usefulness of different <strong>data</strong> displays, for example jointly creating simple column graphs and picture graphs to represent different types of items*
  * *exploring and creating graphs to represent classroom <strong>data</strong>, for example collecting <strong>data</strong> on the country of birth of each student and presenting the results as a picture graph*
  * *using <strong>digital systems</strong> to organise <strong>data</strong> to improve meaning, for example using word processing software to create a list of tasks or visualisation software to create a mind map (diagram) showing relationships between characters in a story*
  * *using common software to present <strong>data</strong> creatively, for example as a slideshow, movie, sounds, image, chart, word art, poster or drawing*
* **Science 1**: Use informal measurements to collect and record observations, using <strong>digital technologies</strong> as appropriate (ACSIS026)
* **Science 2**: Use informal measurements to collect and record observations, using <strong>digital technologies</strong> as appropriate (ACSIS039)

##### Elaborations only

* <span class="light">**Media F-2**: Use media technologies to capture and edit images, sounds and text for a purpose (ACAMAM055)</span>
  * *experimenting with and managing a <strong>digital camera</strong> to capture still or moving images, for example, reviewing captured images, zooming in and out and deleting unwanted images*
  * *experimenting with sound recording technology and found objects to create and record sound effects to support a story*
* <span class="light">**DT F-2**: Recognise and explore <strong>digital systems</strong> (hardware and software components) for a purpose (ACTDIK001)</span>
  * *exploring and using <strong>digital systems</strong> for downloading and storing <strong>information</strong>, for example knowing how to download images from a <strong>website</strong> and inserting them into a document; saving and retrieving <strong>data</strong>*
  * *recognising and using hardware and software components of <strong>digital systems</strong> and experimenting with their functions, for example playing with interactive toys and robotic devices to determine which ones can work with other devices*
* <span class="light">**DT F-2**: Recognise and explore patterns in <strong>data</strong> and represent <strong>data</strong> as pictures, symbols and diagrams (ACTDIK002)</span>
  * *sorting objects and events based on easily identified characteristics and using <strong>digital systems</strong> to represent patterns in <strong>data</strong>, for example sorting birthdates and presenting the patterns using seasonal symbols*

#### **Level 3**: manage and maintain digital data using common methods

##### Content descriptions

* **Media 3-4**: Use media technologies to create time and space through the manipulation of images, sounds and text to tell stories (ACAMAM059)
* **Science 3**: Consider the elements of fair tests and use formal measurements and <strong>digital technologies</strong> as appropriate, to make and record observations accurately (ACSIS055)
  * *using a variety of tools to make observations, such as <strong>digital cameras</strong>, thermometers, rulers and scales*
* **Science 4**: Consider the elements of fair tests and use formal measurements and <strong>digital technologies</strong> as appropriate, to make and record observations accurately (ACSIS066)

##### Elaborations only

* <span class="light">**HASS 3**: Record, sort and represent <strong>data</strong> and the location of places and their characteristics in different formats, including simple graphs, tables and maps, using discipline-appropriate conventions
 (ACHASSI054)</span>
  * *using <strong>information</strong> technologies to record and organise <strong>information</strong> in tables, <strong>data</strong>bases and <strong>digital concept</strong> maps (for example, creating a consequence chart to show what happens when school rules are not followed, or when human settlement damages a component of the natural environment)*
  * *creating tables or picture and column graphs to show patterns in <strong>data</strong> collected from observations or other sources (for example, to show similarities and differences between places; the results of class votes on issues or decisions, participation in community activities, number of local monuments)*
* <span class="light">**DT 3-4**: Collect, access and present different types of <strong>data</strong> using simple software to create <strong>information</strong> and solve problems (ACTDIP009)</span>
  * *recognising that all types of <strong>data</strong> are stored in <strong>digital systems</strong> and may be represented in different ways such as files and folders with names and icons*
* <span class="light">**DT 3-4**: Define simple problems, and describe and follow a sequence of steps and decisions (algorithms) needed to solve them (ACTDIP010)</span>
  * *explaining to others how to follow technical instructions, for example how to capture and download images from a mobile device*
  * *defining and describing the sequence of steps needed to incorporate multiple types of <strong>data</strong> in a solution, for example sequencing the steps in selecting and downloading images and audio to create a book trailer*
* <span class="light">**DT 3-4**: Explain how student solutions and existing <strong>information</strong> systems meet common personal, school or community needs (ACTDIP012)</span>
  * *investigating how <strong>information</strong> systems are used in communities and explaining what needs are being met, for example students jointly creating a short survey and collecting <strong>data</strong> about how many community residents use the online library borrowing system to download e-books and why they do or do not*
* <span class="light">**DT 3-4**: Plan, create and communicate ideas and <strong>information</strong> independently and with others, applying agreed ethical and social protocols
 (ACTDIP013)</span>
  * *considering ways of managing the use of social media to maintain privacy needs, for example activating privacy settings to avoid divulging personal <strong>data</strong> such as photographs, addresses, and names and recognising that all <strong>digital interactions</strong> are difficult to erase (<strong>digital footprints</strong>)*
  * *managing a project that involves students working together to publish online, for example identifying how group members can help each other to avoid delays in finishing the project*

#### **Level 4**: manage and maintain data on different storage mediums – locally and on networks

##### Content descriptions

* **DT 5-6**: Examine the main components of common <strong>digital systems</strong> and how they may connect together to form networks to transmit <strong>data</strong>
 (ACTDIK014)
  * *describing <strong>digital systems</strong> as having internal and external components that perform different functions, for example external components for inputting <strong>data</strong> including keyboard, microphone, stylus; internal processing components including the central processing unit; external output components including speakers, projector, screen; and <strong>data</strong> and <strong>information</strong> storage components including cloud and external devices*
  * *explaining how <strong>data</strong> may be transmitted between two <strong>digital systems</strong> in different ways, for example that wires or cables are used in wired networks to transfer <strong>data</strong> from one <strong>digital system</strong> to another, and radio waves are used to transmit <strong>data</strong> in wireless or mobile networks*
  * *investigating how the internal and external components of <strong>digital systems</strong> are coordinated to handle <strong>data</strong>, for example how a keyboard, central processing unit and screen work together to accept, manipulate and present <strong>data</strong> and <strong>information</strong>*
* **DT 5-6**: Examine how whole numbers are used to represent all <strong>data</strong> in <strong>digital systems</strong> (ACTDIK015)
  * *recognising that <strong>digital systems</strong> represent all types of <strong>data</strong> using number codes that ultimately are patterns of 1s and 0s (called binary digits, which is why they are called <strong>digital systems</strong>)*
* **DT 5-6**: Plan, create and communicate ideas and <strong>information</strong>, including collaboratively online, applying agreed ethical, social and technical protocols (ACTDIP022)
  * *considering ways of managing the use of social media to maintain privacy needs, for example activating privacy settings to avoid divulging personal <strong>data</strong> such as photographs, addresses and names*
* **Science 5**: Decide variables to be changed and measured in fair tests, and observe measure and record <strong>data</strong> with accuracy using <strong>digital technologies</strong> as appropriate (ACSIS087)
  * *recording <strong>data</strong> in tables and diagrams or electronically as <strong>digital images</strong> and spreadsheets*
* **Science 6**: Decide variables to be changed and measured in fair tests, and observe measure and record <strong>data</strong> with accuracy using <strong>digital technologies</strong> as appropriate (ACSIS104)
  * *using <strong>digital technologies</strong> to make accurate measurements and to record <strong>data</strong>*

##### Elaborations only

* <span class="light">**DT 5-6**: Define problems in terms of <strong>data</strong> and functional requirements drawing on previously solved problems (ACTDIP017)</span>
  * *using and interpreting <strong>data</strong>, establishing the root cause of a problem, for example using an annotated diagram to identify omissions, duplications or mismatches of <strong>data</strong>*
* <span class="light">**Science 6**: Construct and use a range of representations, including tables and graphs, to represent and describe observations, patterns or relationships in <strong>data</strong> using <strong>digital technologies</strong> as appropriate (ACSIS107)</span>
  * *using <strong>digital technologies</strong> to construct representations, including dynamic representations*

#### **Level 5**: manage and maintain data for groups of users using a variety of methods and systems

##### Content descriptions

* **DT 7-8**: Investigate how <strong>data</strong> is transmitted and secured in wired, wireless and mobile networks, and how the specifications affect performance (ACTDIK023)
* **DT 7-8**: Analyse and visualise <strong>data</strong> using a range of software to create <strong>information</strong>, and use structured <strong>data</strong> to model objects or events (ACTDIP026)
  * *using features and functions of software to summarise <strong>data</strong> to create <strong>information</strong>, for example calculating a simple budget of income and payments and creating a summary table for analysis*
  * *visualising <strong>data</strong> to create <strong>information</strong>, for example identify trends and outlier <strong>data</strong> from spreadsheets using plots, or displaying geocoded <strong>data</strong> on a map*
  * *applying a set of conditions to a spreadsheet to organise and filter <strong>data</strong>, for example using conditional formatting to highlight the state of particular cells, and filtering and sorting categorical <strong>data</strong> using column filters*
  * *querying an existing <strong>data</strong>base to extract <strong>data</strong> for analysis, for example devising multiple selection criteria or using simple structured query language (SQL) SELECT statements to select records and retrieve specified fields*
* **DT 7-8**: Plan and manage projects that create and communicate ideas and <strong>information</strong> collaboratively online, taking safety and social contexts into account (ACTDIP032)
* **Science 8**: Communicate ideas, findings and evidence based solutions to problems using scientific language, and representations, using <strong>digital technologies</strong> as appropriate (ACSIS148)
  * *using <strong>digital technologies</strong> to construct a range of text types to present science ideas*

##### Elaborations only

* <span class="light">**Science 7**: Measure and control variables, select equipment appropriate to the task and collect <strong>data</strong> with accuracy (ACSIS126)</span>
  * *using a <strong>digital camera</strong> to record observations and compare images using <strong>information</strong> technologies*
* <span class="light">**Science 7**: Construct and use a range of representations, including graphs, keys and models to represent and analyse patterns or relationships in <strong>data</strong> using <strong>digital technologies</strong> as appropriate (ACSIS129)</span>
  * *using spreadsheets to aid the presentation and simple analysis of <strong>data</strong>*
* <span class="light">**Science 7**: Communicate ideas, findings and evidence based solutions to problems using scientific language, and representations, using <strong>digital technologies</strong> as appropriate (ACSIS133)</span>
  * *using <strong>digital technologies</strong> to access <strong>information</strong> and to communicate and collaborate with others on and off site*

#### **Level 6**: manage and maintain data securely in a variety of storage mediums and formats

##### Content descriptions

* **DT 9-10**: Investigate the role of hardware and software in managing, controlling and securing the movement of and access to <strong>data</strong> in networked <strong>digital systems</strong> (ACTDIK034)
  * *explaining how an operating system manages the relationship between hardware, applications and system software*
  * *explaining the role of hardware and software components in allowing people to interact with <strong>digital systems</strong>, for example using a mouse or touch pad or screen, speech, accelerometer*
* **DT 9-10**: Analyse simple compression of <strong>data</strong> and how content <strong>data</strong> are separated from presentation (ACTDIK035)
  * *explaining how simple compression schemes reduce the size of repetitive <strong>data</strong>, for example how run length encoding reduces the size of images*
  * *explaining the difference between lossy and lossless compression, for example the difference between JPEG and PNG images*
* **DT 9-10**: Analyse and visualise <strong>data</strong> to create <strong>information</strong> and address complex problems, and model processes, entities and their relationships using structured <strong>data</strong>
 (ACTDIP037)
  * *summarising <strong>data</strong> using advanced filtering and grouping techniques, for example pivot tables in spreadsheets and aggregation functions in <strong>data</strong>bases*
  * *automating calculations, for example using absolute cell referencing to automatically extend formulas, and automating arithmetic calculations using built-in functions such as trigonometry, compound interest*
  * *simulating simple, iterative processes, for example modelling compound interest or ecological models using a spreadsheet*
  * *documenting the attributes of complex objects and processes using a <strong>data</strong> dictionary*
* **DT 9-10**: Create interactive solutions for sharing ideas and <strong>information</strong> online, taking into account safety, social contexts and legal responsibilities (ACTDIP043)
  * *investigating legal responsibilities of organisations regarding the storage, communication and disposal of personal and organisational <strong>data</strong>, for example the Australian Privacy Principles as they apply to intellectual property*
  * *applying techniques to make ethical decisions when faced with dilemmas about security and ownership of <strong>data</strong>, for example selecting an action that results in the greatest benefit for the most number of people; avoiding the use of photos of deceased persons from Aboriginal and Torres Strait Islander communities*
  * *creating online interactive solutions for working with others by combining or modifying online software tools to support project work*
* **DT 9-10**: Plan and manage projects using an iterative and collaborative approach, identifying risks and considering safety and sustainability (ACTDIP044)
  * *investigating indicators of economic success, for example the capacity to scale up an innovative solution to meet the demands of a mass market and the savings accrued through sustainable practices*
  * *investigating major causes of threats to <strong>data</strong>, for example human actions such as losing a storage device, disclosing passwords, theft and fraud*

##### Elaborations only

* <span class="light">**DT 9-10**: Develop techniques for acquiring, storing and validating quantitative and qualitative <strong>data</strong> from a range of sources, considering privacy and security requirements (ACTDIP036)</span>
  * *developing strategies and techniques for capturing accurate and usable qualitative and quantitative <strong>data</strong> of different formats, for example using text entry for open-ended questions to acquire qualitative <strong>data</strong>; using radio buttons or checkboxes for closed questions to acquire quantitative <strong>data</strong>*
  * *identifying strengths and weaknesses of collecting <strong>data</strong> using different methods, for example online surveys, face-to-face interviews, phone interviews, observation, blog entries in response to a posting, phone logs, browser history and online webcam systems*
  * *developing strategies to ensure the privacy and security of survey <strong>data</strong>, for example using numbers rather than names as identifiers; password protecting files to reduce risks of modifying <strong>data</strong> and using CAPTCHA™ to confirm human responses*
  * *extracting specific <strong>data</strong> from an external source and storing it in a format that is more useful for analysis, for example combining mapping <strong>data</strong> from multiple electronic <strong>data</strong> sets to build a composite representation*
* <span class="light">**Science 9**: Plan, select and use appropriate investigation types, including field work and laboratory experimentation, to collect reliable <strong>data</strong>; assess risk and address ethical issues associated with these methods (ACSIS165)</span>
  * *using modelling and simulations, including using <strong>digital technology</strong> to investigate situations and events*
* <span class="light">**Science 10**: Plan, select and use appropriate investigation types, including field work and laboratory experimentation, to collect reliable <strong>data</strong>; assess risk and address ethical issues associated with these methods (ACSIS199)</span>
  * *using modelling and simulations, including using <strong>digital technology</strong>, to investigate situations and events*
